## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task models the instantaneous rate of population change dP/dt as a function of time t and current population size P, a central theme in population ecology where growth laws incorporate density-dependent feedback, time-varying environments, and nonlinear regulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited intrinsic growth)
- Logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (density-dependent regulation with a carrying capacity c0/c1)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (log(c1) - log(P)) (asymmetric sigmoid growth, often for slow‑aging populations)
- Theta‑logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (generalized logistic with curvature parameter c2 > 1)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (bistability with extinction threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - c3) (reduced, but always positive, growth at low density)
- Seasonal growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) (periodic environment modulating intrinsic growth)
- Logistic with seasonal carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (time‑varying resource saturation)
- Density‑dependent mortality with saturation: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 / (P + c2) (type‑II functional response in mortality)
- Power‑law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (sub‑ or super‑exponential growth, e.g., c1 < 1 for fractal resource acquisition)
- von Bertalanffy‑inspired growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (metabolic scaling applied to population biomass equivalent)
- Time‑dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (exponentially changing resource ceiling)
- Closed‑season harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 - c2 * P * step(t - c3) (piecewise intervention at time c3)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density‑dependent regulation → negative quadratic or higher‑order term in P (e.g., -c1*P**2) that causes growth to decline with abundance
- Allee threshold → a low‑density root where growth becomes negative, expressed as a factor (P - c) in the growth rate
- Carrying capacity → expression (1 - c*P) or (K - P) that makes dP/dt vanish at a finite positive equilibrium
- Time‑varying forcing → periodic sin/cos or slowly varying functions of t lead to limit cycles or transient tracking in population size
- Asymmetric sigmoid → logarithmic term log(c/P) giving a skewed inflection point, typical of long‑lived organisms
- Curvature parameter → exponent c in the theta‑logistic controls the abruptness of density dependence near carrying capacity
- Saturation of mortality → rational form P/(P + c) or 1/(1 + c*P) in a negative term reflects handling‑limited predation
- Piecewise interventions → step(t - c) or max(t - c, 0) terms represent pulsed harvest or sudden habitat change
- Metabolic scaling → allometric exponent (e.g., P**(2/3)) arises when population resource use scales sub‑linearly with body mass
- Oscillatory decay toward equilibrium → products of periodic and damped terms, e.g., exp(-c*t)*sin(...), hint at transient cycles in a relaxing population
